22/08/23, 9:27â€¯am - Brijesh Rakhshiya: Dear all
As per the ISRO official website, they are broadcasting the Live Landing of Chandrayan-3 mission on August 23, 2023, starting from 17:27 Hrs. IST (5:27 PM).

ğŸŒ–ğŸ‡®ğŸ‡³ğŸ›°ï¸

[22/08, 07:05] Dr Sanjay R Joshi: *Chandrayaan 3 update :-*

The powered descent of Vikram Lander is expected to start on Wednesday, August 23, 2023 around 5:47 pm IST..

Expected touch down will be at 6:04 pm (this is modified timing than earlier declared plan)

These last 15 mins of descent are known as *"15 mins of horror"* in ISRO circle. 

*Why??*

Because in this phase Chandrayaan 3 which is in horizontal orientation in about 25 km orbit, will start moving towards the surface of moon at a speed of around *6000 km/hr*, will change its orientation to vertical as it approaches the lunar surface and reduce its speeds to max *3 km/hr* using on-board 4 rockets (in Chandrayaan 2 there were 5) and thursters.

At the height of around 100 metres from ground it will scan the surface and search and select a safe landing place and move towards it using above mentioned Propulsion systems and finally soft land on the moon (all this while by keeping balancing forces in check to keep itself in intended position) and then release Pragyan Rover from its belly to conduct various experiments...

*Sounds exciting ??*

All this final manoeuvering will be fully autonomous, run by on board Computers using various algorithms which are fed into it before lift off..

Its autonomous because it will itself choose which algorithm to use depending on the data it collects at that time. (ISRO command centre won't be able to handle these commands live as these are all split second decisions to be made and the command from earth takes 2.4 to 2.7 seconds to travel to the moon)

It has been fed detailed map of moon surface (4 km Ã— 4.5 kms) where it intends to land. (Chandrayaan 2 was given 500 mts Ã— 500 mts map of then proposed landing site)

There are so many ifs and buts in all these events and we don't know the unknown unknowns in this entire endeavour..

Because of this , last 15 mins of Lander descent are totally unpredictable and hence called as "last 15 mins of horror".

At present It's  systems are being checked and checked again as we speak.

Infact, Chandrayaan 3 is all set to land and start this final phase on the click of button from ISRO command centre even now this minute. 

*Then why are we waiting for 23rd August ??*

Its because the site at which Chandrayaan 3 is planned to land is in dark at present (One lunar night is 14 days duration).. if we land now, the Spacecraft will be deprived off solar energy ..

So we are waiting for dawn (1st light of 14 days sunshine) at landing site...!

*This eagerly awaited event will be broadcast live on Wednesday, August 23, 2023 from 5:27 pm IST on multiple platforms including ISRO website, Its YouTube channel and facebook page, and DD National TV*

So don't miss it... block the day, date and time - Wednesday,  23rd August 2023 starting from 5:27 pm IST for this *grand finale !*

*Don't miss the chance to witness something historical...* 

Remember your grand children will ask you about this day ..

23/11/23, 1:07â€¯pm - Brijesh Rakhshiya: #include <WiFi.h>
#include <WiFiClient.h>
#include <WiFiAP.h>

#define LED_BUILTIN 2   // Led Signal Pin

// Set these to your wifi access point credentials.
const char *ssid = "yourAP";
const char *password = "yourPassword";

WiFiServer server(80);


void setup() {
  pinMode(LED_BUILTIN, OUTPUT);

  Serial.begin(115200);
  Serial.println();
  Serial.println("Configuring access point...");

  // You can remove the password parameter if you want the AP to be open.
  WiFi.softAP(ssid, password);
  IPAddress myIP = WiFi.softAPIP();
  Serial.print("AP IP address: ");
  Serial.println(myIP);
  server.begin();

  Serial.println("Server started");
}

void loop() {
  WiFiClient client = server.available();   // listen for incoming clients

  if (client) {                             // if you get a client,
    Serial.println("New Client.");           // print a message out the serial port
    String currentLine = "";                // make a String to hold incoming data from the client
    while (client.connected()) {            // loop while the client's connected
      if (client.available()) {             // if there's bytes to read from the client,
        char c = client.read();             // read a byte, then
        Serial.write(c);                    // print it out the serial monitor
        if (c == '\n') {                    // if the byte is a newline character

          // if the current line is blank, you got two newline characters in a row.
          // that's the end of the client HTTP request, so send a response:
          if (currentLine.length() == 0) {
            // HTTP headers always start with a response code (e.g. HTTP/1.1 200 OK)
            // and a content-type so the client knows what's coming, then a blank line:
            client.println("HTTP/1.1 200 OK");
            client.println("Content-type:text/html");
            client.println();

            // the content of the HTTP response follows the header:
            client.print("Click <a href=\"/H\">here</a> to turn ON the LED.<br>");
            client.print("Click <a href=\"/L\">here</a> to turn OFF the LED.<br>");

            // The HTTP response ends with another blank line:
            client.println();
            // break out of the while loop:
            break;
          } else {    // if you got a newline, then clear currentLine:
            currentLine = "";
          }
        } else if (c != '\r') {  // if you got anything else but a carriage return character,
          currentLine += c;      // add it to the end of the currentLine
        }

        // Check to see if the client request was "GET /H" or "GET /L":
        if (currentLine.endsWith("GET /H")) {
          digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, HIGH);               // GET /H turns the LED on
        }
        if (currentLine.endsWith("GET /L")) {
          digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, LOW);                // GET /L turns the LED off
        }
      }
    }
    // close the connection:
    client.stop();
    Serial.println("Client Disconnected.");
  }
}

21/11/24, 10:36â€¯am - Yug Thummar: Question 1: Library Management System

Scenario: You are tasked with implementing a simple library management system.

Requirements:

Create a base class Book with title, author, and ISBN fields. Provide appropriate methods to set and get these properties.

Derive a class EBook from Book with an additional field fileSize (in MB). Implement methods to set and get the fileSize.

Create an interface LibraryOperations with methods addBook(Book book) and findBookByTitle(String title). Implement this interface in a class Library which uses an ArrayList<Book> to manage the books.

Demonstrate the use of this and super keywords where applicable.

Handle possible exceptions such as NullPointerException and IllegalArgumentException in your methods.

Requirements:

Implement the classes and methods in Java.

Write a main method to test the functionality of adding and retrieving books from the library.
===============================================================================

Question 2: Dynamic String Operations

Scenario: You need to implement a text manipulation utility.

Requirements:

Create a class TextManipulator with a method reverseWords(String input) that reverses the order of words in a given string. Use StringBuilder for efficient manipulation.

Implement another method removeDuplicateChars(String input) that removes duplicate characters from a string using StringBuffer.

Include exception handling for cases where the input string might be null or empty.

Requirements:

Implement the class and methods in Java.

Write a main method to demonstrate the functionality of reversing words and removing duplicates.
===============================================================================

Question 3: Generics and Collections

Scenario: You are working with a collection of different types of items.

Requirements:

Create a generic class Storage<T> that can store and retrieve items of any type.

Implement methods addItem(T item) and getItem(int index). Use an ArrayList<T> to store the items.

Create a specific instance of Storage to hold Integer items and another instance to hold String items.

Demonstrate how to use these instances by adding and retrieving items, and handle cases where the index might be out of bounds.

Requirements:

Implement the generic class and methods in Java.

Write a main method to test the functionality of storing and retrieving different types of items.
===============================================================================

Question 4: Inheritance and Interfaces

Scenario: You are implementing a payment processing system.

Requirements:

Create an abstract class Payment with methods processPayment(double amount) and getPaymentDetails().

Derive classes CreditCardPayment and PayPalPayment from Payment. Implement specific behaviour for each payment type.

Define an interface Transaction with a method executeTransaction(Payment payment).

Implement this interface in a class TransactionProcessor that processes the payment by invoking processPayment and prints payment details.

Requirements:

Implement the abstract class, derived classes, and interface in Java.

Write a main method to demonstrate how to process different types of payments using TransactionProcessor.
===============================================================================

Question 5: Exception Handling and Access Specifiers

Scenario: You are developing a simple calculator application.

Requirements:

Create a class Calculator with methods for basic arithmetic operations: add, subtract, multiply, and divide.

Ensure that the divide method handles division by zero by throwing an ArithmeticException.

Use access specifiers to control the visibility of methods and fields.

Implement a method performOperation(String operation, double a, double b) that uses a switch statement to call the appropriate arithmetic method and handles any exceptions that might be thrown.

Requirements:

Implement the class and methods in Java.

Write a main method to test the calculator with different operations and handle any exceptions that arise.

1: Bank Account Manager


Scenario:


You are tasked with developing a
system for managing bank accounts. Each account can be a Savings Account or a
Current Account, and customers should be able to deposit or withdraw money. A
minimum balance must be maintained in Savings Accounts.


Requirements:


Create classes BankAccount, SavingsAccount, and CurrentAccount.
Implement methods to deposit and withdraw money with
proper validation.
Withdrawals should be denied if they cause the balance
to drop below the minimum required for Savings Accounts.
Use inheritance to extend functionality from BankAccount
to SavingsAccount and CurrentAccount.
Use this and super to refer to class
members.
Implement Exception Handling to handle cases
like insufficient balance.



Constraints:


Minimum balance for Savings Account is 1000 units.
Withdrawal from a Current Account cannot go below 0.
Use StringBuilder to create transaction history.
Apply proper access specifiers for fields and
methods.



Sample
Input:


Account Type: Savings


Initial Deposit: 5000


Action: Withdraw 2000

Sample Output:

Transaction
Successful. New Balance: 3000






 ============================================================


Question
2: Library Book Issue System


Scenario:


Design a program for a library to
manage book issuance to users. The system should allow users to issue and
return books.


Requirements:


Create a class Book with details like title, author, and ISBN.
Create a class User that can issue and return books.
Use an interface Issueable to define methods for issuing and returning books.
Use Generics to manage the list of books issued
to a user.
Handle scenarios where a book might already be issued
to another user (throw a custom exception).



Constraints:


The system should not issue more than 5 books to a user
at a time.
Use Array or ArrayList to store issued
books.
Ensure encapsulation by using appropriate access
specifiers for the fields.



Sample
Input:

User: John Doe

Action: Issue
Book (ISBN: 123456)

Sample Output:

Book Issued
Successfully. Books Issued: 1






 ===================================================================


Question
3: Employee Management System


Scenario:


Create a system to manage employees
in a company. Employees can be of different types: permanent and
contract-based. Each employee should have a name, ID, and salary. Permanent
employees get additional benefits based on their base salary.


Requirements:


Create a base class Employee with attributes like name, ID, and salary.
Create subclasses PermanentEmployee and ContractEmployee, and apply inheritance to implement specific
salary calculations.
Use this keyword in constructors to differentiate class
variables and parameters.
Use StringBuffer to manage employee data in a
thread-safe manner.
Implement Exception Handling for invalid salary
values.



Constraints:


Permanent employees get a 10% bonus on their base
salary.
Contract employees do not get bonuses.
The salary cannot be less than 3000 units.



Sample
Input:

Employee Type:

Permanent Name:
Alice

Base Salary:
4000

Sample Output:

Employee Alice
added with total salary: 4400






 ============================================================


Question
4: Multithreaded Order Processor


Scenario:


Create a system for processing
online orders. Multiple threads should process different orders simultaneously,
and each order should calculate the total price of items.


Requirements:


Use multithreading to process multiple orders
concurrently.
Each thread should process an order, calculating the
total price of items.
Use static variables to maintain the total
number of orders processed.
Apply String operations to generate order
summaries.
Demonstrate synchronization to handle concurrent
order processing.



Constraints:


Each order can contain up to 5 items.
Ensure that no two threads update the order count
simultaneously.
Use Exception Handling to handle cases where
item prices are invalid (e.g., negative prices).



Sample
Input:

Order 1: Item1
(200), Item2 (300), Item3 (150)

Order 2: Item1
(100), Item2 (250)

Sample Output:

Order 1 Total:
650

Order 2 Total:
350

Total Orders
Processed: 2






 ==========================================================================


Question
5: Vehicle Rental Service


Scenario:


Develop a vehicle rental service
system that handles different types of vehicles. Customers can rent and return
vehicles, and the system must track availability and rentals.


Requirements:


Create classes Vehicle, Car, and Bike to represent different types of vehicles. Use inheritance
where applicable.
Implement an interface Rentable
that defines methods for renting and returning vehicles.
Use Generics to manage a list of rented
vehicles.
Implement StringBuilder to build dynamic vehicle
descriptions and rental history.
Handle exceptions when trying to rent a vehicle that is
already rented.



Constraints:


The system can handle a maximum of 10 vehicles.
Use this keyword to refer to instance variables
inside constructors and methods.
Use the static keyword to maintain a count of
the total number of vehicles rented.



Sample
Input:

Vehicle Type:
Car

Action: Rent

Sample Output:

Car rented
successfully. Total vehicles rented: 1
